## 2026-06-26T102800Z — PASS — partnership-desktop-message-button
- Pages: /partnerships/[id]
- What: **Desktop users can now message a partnership owner directly from the listing page.** Previously, the desktop "Interested?" sidebar card showed only "Send Email" + phone. Mobile had the "Message" button in the sticky bar. Now the desktop sidebar card also shows a dark "Message" button (above Email/phone) — clicking it creates or opens a thread at `/messages/[threadId]` when signed in, redirects to auth when not. The button is hidden when viewing your own listing or when the listing has no `poster_id` (scraped listings without a ClubHanger account), matching mobile behavior exactly. 2 files: `ContactButtons.tsx` (add `posterId` prop, auth state, message handler — mirrors `ContactBar`); `partnerships/[id]/page.tsx` (pass `posterId={p.poster_id}` to `ContactButtons`).
- Goal: feature depth / on-site engagement — `[want]` lane (last 3 non-bug cycles: aircraft-mission-twin-stol [goal], cream-surface-sweep [want], aircraft-for-sale-ai-draft [want] — not all 3 [want], so [want] owed per 3:1 policy). Completes the on-site messaging feature for desktop — the desktop/mobile asymmetry was the only remaining gap in the messaging story. Pageviews at orient: 404 last 7d (PostHog secondary; GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).

## 2026-06-25T101126Z — PASS — message-notify-throttle
- Pages: /messages, /messages/[threadId]
- What: **On-site message email notifications are now throttled to at most one per thread per hour.** Previously, every message sent in a conversation triggered an email to the recipient — a rapid back-and-forth exchange could produce an inbox-flooding burst of "You have a new message" emails. Now `notifyMessageRecipient` checks an in-process `MESSAGE_NOTIFY_LAST` Map before sending: if an email was already delivered for this thread within the past hour, it skips silently and the message still saves. The first message after any 1-hour quiet window still fires normally. Same fire-and-forget pattern as before; no user-visible change on a single-message thread.
- Goal: feature quality / defensive UX — `[want]` lane (last 3 non-bug cycles: seeking-drive-time [want], messaging-new-message-email [want], model-curate-cessna-421 [goal] — not all 3 [want], so [want] owed per 3:1 policy). Explicitly queued in messaging-new-message-email CHANGELOG "Next" notes. Pageviews at orient: 374 last 7d (PostHog secondary; GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING). Pure server-side change: 1 file (`src/app/actions.ts`), ~17 lines added — a module-level `Map<string, number>` (threadId → last-sent timestamp) + one guard block at the top of `notifyMessageRecipient`. Same in-process pattern as `AI_DRAFT_CALLS`; effective for current traffic / warm-instance reuse; swap for Redis/KV if traffic grows significantly.
- Goal-lane: [want]
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260625T101126Z-message-notify-throttle.md
- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` compiled clean (exit 0, no TypeScript errors). QA smoke (`next start` production build on port 3020, NOT dev) — exit 0 on `/messages`, `/partnerships/seeking`, `/aircraft` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 (6/6 — HTTP 200, zero app-origin console errors, zero horizontal overflow). Non-visual cycle (server-side logic only, no UI change) — screenshots saved as audit trail, not read.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/message-notify-throttle/
- Next: (1) Rate limit is in-process — if Vercel cold-starts or traffic spikes, some threads may get a second notification before the Map warms up; swap for a Supabase-backed `last_notified_at` column on `threads` for true durability (additive schema, human DDL). (2) The interval is 1 hour — consider whether 30 min or per-day is the right cadence once the feature is live and the human has set RESEND_API_KEY. (3) The alerts double-opt-in confirmation email (slice 2 of email alerts) is ready to queue next.

- Pages: /partnerships/new, /partnerships/seeking/new
- What: **The "Generate with AI" feature on both posting forms now rejects unauthenticated callers and rate-limits logged-in users to 10 AI draft requests per hour.** Previously, the two server actions (`generatePartnershipDraft`, `generateSeekerDraft`) had no auth check — any caller (including non-logged-in users making direct requests) could trigger Anthropic API calls at will. This completes slice 3 of the "[P2][want] Generate with AI" backlog item (slice 1 = seeking form, slice 2 = partnership form).

Pure server-side change in `actions.ts`: a 24-line `checkAiDraftAccess()` helper (module-level `Map<userId, {count, resetAt}>`) + one `await checkAiDraftAccess()` call at the top of each generation function. Implementation note: rate limit is in-process (module-level Map) — effective for typical Vercel warm-instance reuse at current traffic; swap for Redis/KV if traffic grows.

- What: **Parts listings (cowlings, mags, rivet kits) and no-price listings no longer show up in the aircraft browse, counts, or family pages.** The site had 211 verified sub-$50k listings that were parts/projects — not flyable aircraft — polluting every buyer-facing view: the browse showed "M20C COWLING" and "O-235 MAGS" as aircraft, make/model pages had inflated counts, and the cross-sell card on /partnerships showed an inaccurate total. A global `asking_price >= $50,000` floor is now applied to every buyer-facing aircraft query (browse, make/model/state counts, state rails, market price stats, comp pill price map). The sitemap already had this floor — this brings all buyer surfaces into parity. Partnerships are unaffected (buy-in ≠ aircraft asking price).

## 2026-06-24T12:55Z — PASS — seeker-filter-multi-airport
- Pages: /partnerships/seeking
- What: **The Pilots-Seeking page now lets you filter by more than one home airport at once.** Before, the "Near Home Airport" box took a single ICAO code; now you can type several (e.g. KAUG, KBWI, KCLT) — press Enter, comma, or click away to add each as a small removable chip — and you'll see pilots based at **any** of those airports together. Each chosen airport also shows as a removable chip above the results, so you can drop one without clearing the rest. The "within X miles" radius option now appears only when a single airport is selected (a radius around several airports doesn't make sense). Works the same on desktop and mobile, and existing single-airport links and saved searches keep working unchanged. This mirrors the multi-airport filter already shipped on the main `/partnerships` page.
- Goal: feature depth — `[want]` lane (last non-bug cycle `guide-flying-club-vs-co-ownership` pulled `[goal]` → alternated to `[want]`). On-site pageviews at orient: 325 last 7d (PostHog secondary; GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING). Pure front-end + query-param wiring over the existing `home_airport` column — no schema, no new pages. This is the explicitly-queued "Next" from `partnership-filter-multi-airport` (apply the same multi-airport chip input to the seeking browse filter) and a usability win on an existing priority seed page.

- Verdict: PASS. `npx next build` + typecheck green (pre-existing `.test.ts` tsc errors only, none in touched files). ## 2026-06-24T12:50Z — PASS — guide-flying-club-vs-co-ownership
- Pages: /guides/flying-club-vs-co-ownership, /guides
- What: **New plain-English guide: "Flying Club vs. Aircraft Co-Ownership."** It answers a real question pilots weigh when they want to fly affordably — join a flying club (pay to belong and rent the club's planes) or buy a share of one aircraft with a few partners. The guide compares the two side by side: what you pay and what you build (equity), fleet access vs. one shared plane, who controls the schedule and maintenance, how easy each is to get into and out of, who each suits, and how to decide — with the same honest, "this is not legal/tax/financial advice" framing as the sibling guides. It now shows as a card on the Guides hub and links out to the related guides, the cost calculator, and partnerships.
- Goal: SEO content depth / INDEXING stage — `[goal]` lane (last non-bug cycle `saved-search-inline-rename` pulled `[want]` → alternated to `[goal]`). A genuinely-unique, high-intent indexable page that diversifies off the heavily-worked aircraft-compare family (per its own "DIVERSIFY next" note) and extends the proven "X vs co-ownership" decision-guide pattern (leaseback-vs). Added to the guides hub ItemList JSON-LD + sitemap.

## 2026-06-24T10:21Z — PASS — clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each internal for-sale aircraft page can now show an honest "Good deal / Fair price / Priced high" verdict** — the endorsement-style read the ClubHanger Estimate has been building toward. The existing estimate already said whether a plane is priced **above or below the whole make+model family**, but that alone isn't a fair verdict (a 1976 Cessna 172 is "below" the family median simply because it's old, not because it's a bargain). The new **"Deal check"** line, shown right under the family comparison, fixes that by comparing the asking price **only against similar-year (±5 years) and similar-hours listings of the same make and model** — controlling for the two biggest things that move an airplane's price. So on a real example this run, a **1976 Cessna 172M at $120k** reads **"Below market"** vs all 172s but **"Fair price"** once you look only at other mid-1970s, comparable-hours 172s — a genuinely useful, honest distinction. It states the comp basis and count in plain English ("compared with 4 … listings within ±5 years and comparable total time, median $X"), and shows **nothing at all** when the listing lacks a year or total time, or when there aren't at least 4 truly comparable listings — no made-up verdict on thin data.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow-Zestimate parity, the brand differentiator) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `compare-pairs-expansion` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS → no blocker → [want] owed per the 1:1). This is the remaining slice of the flagship **[P1][want] "ClubHanger Estimate — fair-value pricing"** item, whose backlog note explicitly gated the value verdict on *"once comps are narrowed to year-band + hours (then a value judgement is honest)"* — delivered exactly, and **additively** (the existing whole-family descriptive estimate is untouched). A product win the pageview metric can't see tonight. Honesty-rule-clean: a value judgement is published only on a year+hours-controlled comp set of ≥4, with a ±5% dead band reading "Fair price", whole-dollar/percent only, and an explicit "estimate, not an appraisal" framing; self-suppresses on thin/missing data. Scoreboard at orient: 325 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).
- Spec: nightshift/specs/2026-06-24T10-14-40Z-clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict.md
- Verdict: PASS. Four files, additive. `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.ts` — new pure, import-free `clubHangerDealVerdict(subject, comps)` + exported bands (`MIN_DEAL_COMPS=4`, `DEAL_YEAR_BAND=5`, hours band = max(1,000 hrs, ±35%), `DEAL_DEAD_BAND=5%`); returns null unless the subject has a real price+year+ttaf AND ≥4 comps fall inside both bands. `src/lib/aircraftEstimate.test.ts` — 7 new worked-example tests (good/fair/high, out-of-band exclusion, relative hours band, null on missing year/ttaf, null on thin narrowed set); **12/12 pass** via `node --experimental-strip-types --test`. `src/lib/aircraftForSale.ts` — read-only `getFamilyComps()` (selects year+ttaf, `.neq('id', self)`, same family filter as `getFamilyAskingPrices`, fails soft to []); the two family reads run concurrently via `Promise.all`. `src/app/aircraft/listing/[id]/page.tsx` — additive `DealCheck` sub-block inside `EstimatePanel` (new optional `deal` prop); existing family-median path unchanged. NO schema/DB change, NO new dependency, NO new route. `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 24.4s"); `tsc --noEmit` clean in all touched source files (only the pre-existing `.test.ts` TS5097 import-extension baseline remains). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next start -p 3100`, NOT dev): qa-smoke exit 0 on a real `/aircraft/listing/[id]` (the 1976 C172M above) + `/aircraft` at desktop 1280 + mobile 375 (4/4 — HTTP 200, **zero** app-origin console errors, **zero** horizontal overflow). Read the screenshots: the layered panel renders cleanly at both viewports (family "Below market" then the bordered "Deal check / Fair price" sub-section), single-column on mobile, no overflow. Verified across many SR22/172 listings that the verdict self-suppresses correctly when a listing has no year and/or too few similar-year+hours comps — the honesty floor is doing real work.
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/clubhanger-estimate-deal-verdict/

Nothing about the fields, layout, or how you submit changed — this is purely a safety net so a long, multi-section form never costs you your progress. Two files. **New** `src/components/useFormDraft.ts` — a reusable client hook (written so the parallel Post-a-Seeking form can adopt it) that DOM-drives an uncontrolled `<form>`: snapshots its named text/number/select/textarea fields to `localStorage` (debounced 600ms) on input, restores them on mount, and reports a `status` ('idle'|'saving'|'saved'|'restored'); all storage access is try/catch-wrapped so a full/blocked `localStorage` just no-ops and the form works as before. **Edit** `src/components/PostPartnershipForm.tsx` — `ref`+`onSubmit` wired to the hook, a `DraftIndicator` (Saving…/Draft saved/Draft restored, with `aria-live`) at the form top, and a `useEffect` that clears the draft on a successful post and re-restores it after a failed submit (React 19 resets an uncontrolled `<form action>` once the action resolves — the snapshot taken in `onSubmit` is written back so nothing is lost). The submit/redirect server action (`createPartnership`) was left untouched. `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 23.9s"); `tsc --noEmit` shows zero errors in both touched/new files (only the pre-existing 6-error `.test.ts` baseline remains). ## 2026-06-23T08:35Z — PASS — alerts-double-opt-in
- Pages: /alerts/status, /aircraft (the alert-signup box), plus two new backend routes (/api/alerts/confirm, /api/alerts/unsubscribe)
- What: **Email alerts now use a proper double-opt-in flow — sign up, get a confirmation email, click to confirm, and a working one-click unsubscribe.** Until now, when a visitor entered their email to get alerts for new listings (the "Get alerts for new Cessna 172 listings" box on the for-sale pages), the address was just stored as "pending" with no way to confirm it or opt back out — so we could never actually, responsibly send a single alert. This cycle wires the real flow: a new signup now triggers a confirmation email with a "Confirm my alerts" button and an unsubscribe link; clicking confirm flips the subscription to **confirmed**, clicking unsubscribe flips it to **unsubscribed**, and both land on a clean branded ClubHanger page telling the visitor what happened. The signup box's success message now says "Almost there — check your inbox" instead of implying they're already subscribed. **Nothing actually sends yet** — the email layer is built to send via Resend the moment the human drops in a `RESEND_API_KEY`, and until then every send is a safe logged no-op (so this ships with zero risk of mailing anyone prematurely).
- Goal: feature depth / conversion infrastructure — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `airport-og-card-parity` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). This is **slice 2** of the top **[P1][want] "Email alerts capture"** item; the backlog explicitly says "Build slices 2-3 NOW, gated behind `RESEND_API_KEY` — do NOT block on the key... no-op + log when it's absent," and the double-opt-in schema (`confirm_token`/`confirmed_at`/`unsubscribe_token`) is already migrated. Slice 1 (capture UI + pending insert) shipped earlier. A list-building / conversion win the pageview metric can't see tonight; it's the prerequisite that makes the list legally sendable (CAN-SPAM/GDPR confirmed opt-in + one-click unsubscribe). Honesty-rule-clean: no fabricated content, no actual sends without a key, soft-fails on bad tokens. Scoreboard at orient: 148 pageviews last 7d (GSC not configured; STAGE=INDEXING).
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260623T082913Z-alerts-double-opt-in.md
- Verdict: PASS. New `src/lib/email.ts` — `sendEmail()` POSTs to the Resend API when `RESEND_API_KEY` is set, else logs `[email:noop]` and returns `{sent:false}` (verified the key is ABSENT in this env, so the no-op path is what runs); plus `buildAlertConfirmEmail()` (HTML + text, escaped). `subscribeToAlerts` now mints `confirm_token`+`unsubscribe_token` in-app (so it can build the email links without reading the row back — anon has no SELECT on `alerts` by design), inserts them, and on a genuinely NEW row sends the confirmation (skips it on a 23505 dedupe so a resubmit can't spam an address). New service-role route handlers `/api/alerts/confirm` + `/api/alerts/unsubscribe` (anon can't UPDATE `alerts`) flip status by token and 307-redirect to the new branded, `noindex` `/alerts/status` page (one page, `?state=confirmed|unsubscribed|invalid`). `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 22.4s"); `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors in all touched files (test-file baseline unchanged). ## 2026-06-23T08:01Z — PASS — clubhanger-estimate-detail
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each for-sale aircraft's own page now shows a "ClubHanger Estimate" — how its asking price compares to the going rate for the same make+model.** Right under the price, a new panel reads the median asking price of every *other* active, priced listing of the same make+model family and tells the buyer, in one line, whether this plane is asking **Below market / Around market / Above market** — e.g. "Above market · Asking $49,900 (40%) above the median Cessna 172 listing", with the comp count and median shown ("Based on the median asking price of N other Cessna 172 listings for sale now") and a link to see the whole family. It's deliberately a **descriptive market comparison, not a "good deal" endorsement**: the comp set is the entire make+model family, so a big gap usually reflects year/hours/avionics rather than a bargain — the panel says exactly that ("actual value also depends on year, hours, and avionics. An estimate, not an appraisal or an offer"). The block only appears when the listing has a real price AND there are at least 4 other priced same-family comps; on no-price, unknown-family, or thin-data listings it simply doesn't render.
- Goal: feature depth / buyer UX (Zillow "Zestimate" analog) — **[want] lane** (last non-bug cycle `home-rail-cards-internal-link` pulled [goal]; last cycle PASS so no blocker, so [want] was owed per the 1:1). ## 2026-06-23T07:31Z — PASS — listing-cost-and-price-history
- Pages: /aircraft/listing/[id]
- What: **Each for-sale aircraft's own page now shows an "Estimated cost to own" and (when the price has actually moved) a "Price history" block** — the Zillow/Redfin pattern the backlog asks for. The **cost-to-own** block gives a buyer a quick, honest ballpark of what owning the plane outright runs per month/year: insurance (≈1% of the asking price, the one line that scales with this specific aircraft), plus clearly-labeled *typical* figures for hangar/tie-down, the annual inspection, and operating (fuel + reserves at ~$150/hr over an assumed 75 hrs/yr). It carries a plain "rough estimate — your costs will vary" disclaimer and a link to the full cost calculator so buyers can plug in their own numbers — nothing is presented as listing-specific that isn't. The **price-history** block only appears when we have a real recorded price change: it shows the change date, the new price, the signed delta + % (e.g. "−$5,000 (−4%)"), and the original price struck through; listings with no recorded change show no block (no empty filler). No-price listings show neither.

- What: **Cleared the filed "airport pages return HTTP 500" blocker and gave the whole site a proper, branded error page.** First, the investigation: the previous cycle reported that `/airports/khwd` and `/aircraft/cessna/172` returned a 500 on a local production build, with the real error hidden behind a "missing chunk" error. On a **clean** build (`rm -rf .next && build && start`) **none of it reproduces** — `/airports/{khwd,kpao,koak,ksql,kccr,klvk,kapc}`, five different `/aircraft/<make>/<model>` pages, and `/partnerships/near/khwd` all return 200 with real content, and **production (clubhanger.com) returns 200 on all of them too.** So the 500 was a stale local build-cache artifact, not a real bug and not a production outage — the sitemap'd airport/model pages are healthy. Second, the real fix to the part that *was* a problem (the error being *hidden*): the site previously had **no custom error page at all**, so any unexpected error fell back to a blank/broken default. It now shows a friendly branded "Something went wrong" page (warning icon, a "Try again" button, and a "Go home" link, inside the normal nav + footer) — and the underlying error is now logged instead of swallowed. Nothing about any normal page changed.
- Goal: blocker/[bug] — resolves the standing `[P1][bug]` (airport/model 500), which the allocation policy takes first, uncapped. - Verdict: PASS. Two additive files only — `src/app/error.tsx` (client segment boundary: branded fallback inside the root layout, `reset()` "Try again" + home link, logs the error + shows its `digest`) and `src/app/global-error.tsx` (root-layout boundary with its own inline-styled `<html>`/`<body>`; makes the app **own** the `global-error` build chunk instead of relying on Next's default — the default's chunk is exactly what went missing as the `ChunkLoadError` that masked the real error). No existing page/route/data/component touched; no schema/DB/SQL; no new dependency; no FREEZE file. `npx next build` green; `tsc --noEmit` clean (only the pre-existing `.test.ts` baseline errors). ## 2026-06-22T12:32Z — PASS — sitemap-lastmod
- Pages: /sitemap.xml (affects the lastmod of /, /aircraft, /partnerships, all make/model/state/near/airport programmatic pages)
- What: **Every programmatic and index page in our sitemap now carries a real "last updated" date, so Google has a genuine freshness signal it can use to decide what to re-crawl.** Until now only individual partnership listings had a date; the homepage, `/aircraft`, `/partnerships`, and all ~250 make/model/state/near-airport/airport landing pages had none at all. This cycle each of those pages gets an honest `<lastmod>` derived from when its underlying listings actually changed — the aircraft-for-sale pages use the newest for-sale-listing date, the partnership pages use the newest partnership-update date, and the homepage uses the later of the two. The date reflects real data changes (it stays put across deploys when nothing changed), so it's a truthful signal, not fake daily churn. The static guides/tools/about pages deliberately get **no** date (we don't fake a "freshly updated" stamp on copy that didn't change). Nothing about how any page looks or behaves changed — this is pure sitemap/SEO metadata.

## 2026-06-22T11:17Z — PASS — airport-thinpage-prune
- Pages: /airports/[icao] (all airport hub pages), /sitemap.xml
- What: **Stopped ~16,800 near-empty airport pages from polluting our sitemap and Google's index.** We have one hub page per airport (`/airports/KXXX`) for all ~16,885 airports in the database, but only **9** airports actually have an aircraft partnership based there — every other one was a thin, near-identical "No active partnerships based at KXXX yet — Post the first one" page. Until now **all 16,885** were listed in our sitemap as high-priority daily-crawl URLs. That's exactly the kind of thin/doorway-page sprawl Google penalizes, and at our current stage (almost nothing indexed yet) it wastes the crawl budget we want spent on the ~200 pages that actually have content. This cycle: the sitemap now lists **only** airport pages that have a real partnership based there (down from 16,885 to 9 airport URLs; total sitemap 263 URLs), and every other airport page is now marked **"noindex, follow"** — it still loads normally and all its links still work (so Google keeps following them), it just won't be indexed as a thin page. The airport pages that DO have listings (e.g. Palo Alto / KPAO) are completely unchanged and stay fully indexable. Nothing about how any page looks or behaves changed — this is pure SEO hygiene.
- Goal: [goal] — `[P1][goal] Thin-page pruning` (Brainstorm 2026-06-20 §A), the airport family (the biggest thin family by far). Pulled the [goal] lane: the last non-bug cycle (marketplace-cross-sell) was [want] PASS with no blocker, so [goal] was owed per the 1:1. Top INDEXING-stage lever right now — concentrates crawl budget on real content instead of ~16.8k near-duplicate empties; completes the inventory-gating pattern every other programmatic family (make/model/state/near) already had. Judged by leading indicators per the honesty rule (sitemap shrank to inventory-backed URLs; thin pages now noindex,follow), not tonight's pageview delta. ## 2026-06-22T02:23Z — PASS — fix-visitor-webhook-204
- Pages: /aircraft, /, /partnerships (all pages — the bug fired on every page load)
- What: **Fixed a bug that was throwing a server error on every single page load across the whole site.** The real-time "visitor radar" feature (the one that pings Slack when someone visits) has a tiny beacon that every visitor's browser calls on each page. When the Slack credentials aren't set in an environment (which is the case on staging/preview), that beacon was crashing with a 500 error — because it tried to send a "204 No Content" response *with* a body, which isn't allowed. Every visitor was silently logging a red 500 error in their browser console on every page. The fix returns a proper empty 204 instead, so the beacon quietly does nothing when Slack isn't configured (exactly as intended) and the console stays clean. The Slack-alerting behavior, when credentials *are* set (production), is completely unchanged.
- Goal: **[bug] / blocker (uncapped, fixed first).** Not the planned lane pick: this cycle was owed **[want]** (last non-bug cycle, partnership-make-faq, was [goal]), and I had the [want] follow-up — removable active-filter chips on /aircraft — built and green. But QA surfaced this pre-existing sitewide 500 console error, which the allocation policy says to fix **before** anything else (a console error is a blocker) — and critically it was breaking the mandatory QA "zero app-origin console errors" gate for *every* cycle going forward, so it had to land first. The deferred filter-chips work is preserved on branch `night/aircraft-filter-chips` (build-green) for the next [want] cycle. Scoreboard at orient: STAGE=INDEXING (GSC not configured this run), pageviews 114/7d.
- Spec: nightshift/specs/20260622T022343Z-fix-visitor-webhook-204.md
- Verdict: PASS. One line of app code changed in `src/app/api/visitor-webhook/route.ts`: the not-configured early return `NextResponse.json({ ok: false }, { status: 204 })` (which throws `TypeError: Invalid response status code 204` — a 204 must be body-less — and 500s) became `new NextResponse(null, { status: 204 })`. Root-caused from the server log (`Invalid response status code 204`) + confirmed the beacon source (`src/lib/analytics.ts`) and the unset env (`SLACK_BOT_TOKEN`/`SLACK_VISITOR_CHANNEL_ID`). `npx next build` green ("✓ Compiled successfully in 22.7s", 239/239 static pages); `tsc --noEmit` clean (only the 4 pre-existing `.test.ts` baseline errors, 0 in touched files). QA against the PRODUCTION build (`npx next build` + `npm run start`, NOT `next dev`; killed lingering stale port-3000 servers first):
  - **(1) Beacon fixed:** `POST /api/visitor-webhook` (Slack env unset) → **204** (was **500**), no body. ✓
  - **(2) Smoke PASS exit 0:** `/aircraft`, `/`, `/partnerships` × desktop 1280 + mobile 375 → all HTTP 200, **zero** app-origin console errors (the sitewide 500 is gone — it was present on every page before), **zero** horizontal overflow. ✓
  - **(3) No server-side throw during QA:** 0 `Invalid response status code 204` lines in the server log across the full smoke run. ✓
  - **(4) Looks right:** /aircraft desktop + 375px screenshots confirm listings/photos/sidebar/footer render correctly and unchanged (backend-only fix). ✓
- Screenshots: nightshift/screenshots/fix-visitor-webhook-204/
- Next: ship the preserved **active-filter chips on /aircraft** (branch `night/aircraft-filter-chips`, spec 20260622T022343Z-aircraft-filter-chips.md) as the next [want] cycle — removable chips in the results header, build-green, just needs a fresh QA pass + merge.
